Chapter 1 Holiday processing schedule
Mastercard will not perform settlement for any of its customers during certain holiday periods.
Overview settlement U.S. dollar holiday schedule.......................................................................................... 11
Settlement holidays..............................................................................................................................................11

Quick Reference Booklet—Merchant Edition • 3 October 2023 10
Overview settlement U.S. dollar holiday schedule
The Mastercard settlement U.S. dollar holiday schedule is based on the U.S. holidays observed by
the New York Branch Federal Reserve are described in this section.
Settlement holidays
Mastercard Global Settlement Services supports regional settlement service cutoffs on most
U.S. Federal Reserve holidays.
This feature offers customers the ability to settle cross-border and intracurrency activity based
on the holiday schedule of their local settlement bank, with the exception of 1 January and 25
December when no settlement cutoffs are performed.
Settlement bank advisements will be distributed to customers according to the holiday schedule
provided by the local settlement bank or local monetary authority.
Mastercard will not move monies in a Regional Settlement Service on days when the U.S.
Federal Reserve Bank is closed. As a general rule, when U.S. Federal Reserve holidays occur on a
Saturday, Federal Reserve banks and branches will be open the preceding Friday. When U.S.
Federal Reserve holidays occur on a Sunday, all Federal Reserve offices will be closed the
following Monday. See New York Branch Federal Reserve Bank Holidays for specific holiday
dates.
2023 New York Branch Federal Reserve Bank Holidays

Acceptor business codes (MCCs)
© 2023 Mastercard. Proprietary. All rights reserved.
Quick Reference Booklet—Merchant Edition • 3 October 2023 21
Overview
Detailed MCC information is organized in several ways.
• Acceptor business code (MCC) criteria
• Required use of MCCs, transaction category codes, and acceptor business programs
• Added and changed MCCs
• MCCs in numeric, alphabetic, and transaction category code order
• Abbreviated airline names to be used in the Merchant Description in the IPM First
Presentment/1240 message
• Acceptor business programs and associated MCCs
Acceptor business code (MCC) criteria
Mastercard uses various criteria for establishing new acceptor business codes (MCC).
Before customers request new MCCs, they should review this practice to determine whether a
merchant qualifies for a new MCC.
Mastercard uses the following criteria to establish new generic MCCs:
• Projected annual bankcard volume for the MCC must equal at least USD 10 million, and the
new merchant type must be distinct and separate from other industries; or
• Industry transaction characteristics require that the transactions must be identified
specifically in the authorization and clearing systems to maximize Mastercard opportunities
(for example, Payment Transactions).
Mastercard uses the following criteria to establish new travel and entertainment industry
MCCs:
• Projected annual bankcard volume for the MCC must equal at least USD 1 million; and
• The merchant must be listed in an internationally recognized trade directory, for example, the
Official Airline Guide; and
• If the merchant is an airline, the merchant must have 10 or more aircraft in the fleet, or
• If the merchant is a car rental company, the merchant must have 500 or more vehicles, or
• If the merchant is a hotel, the merchant must have in place a preferred usage program for
which cardholders must register, or must have five or more properties or a single property
with 500 or more rooms. If the merchant has multiple properties, then each property must
operate under the same name.
Note that Mastercard grants new MCCs at its sole discretion even if the merchant meets the
above stated criteria.
NOTE: To add, change, or delete an MCC, complete the Acceptor Business Code (MCC) Request Form
(Form 380) available on Mastercard Connect® by selecting Help > Forms.
Acceptor business codes (MCCs)
Overview
© 2023 Mastercard. Proprietary. All rights reserved.
Quick Reference Booklet—Merchant Edition • 3 October 2023 22
Required use of MCCs
MCCs are required in all authorization and clearing messages initiated at a point-of-interaction
location. The MCCs help to accurately reflect the merchant’s primary business and facilitate risk
management.
Acquirers must provide a valid and accurate MCC recognized by Mastercard in Data Element
(DE) 26 (Acceptor Business Code [MCC]) of the IPM First Presentment/1240 message. An
accurate MCC is defined as a valid MCC that most reasonably and fairly describes the
merchant’s primary business. IPM First Presentment/1240 messages submitted with an invalid
MCC will be rejected, and IPM error message 0531, “DE26 ACCEPTOR BUSINESS CODE (MCC)
INVALID OR OBSOLETE,” will appear.
Transactions with MCCs from 3000 through 3350 must supply an abbreviated airline name.
Transaction Category Codes
Transaction Category Codes (TCCs) are required in Mastercard authorization messages and are
used during Stand-In processing.
Mastercard uses the TCC to determine the transaction currency amount that Mastercard will
authorize on behalf of the issuer. The description of each MCC includes the TCCs that are valid
for that MCC. Only a valid combination of MCC and TCC may be used in a transaction.
Definitions: Transaction Category Codes and types of transactions
Each of the Transaction Category Code types and the transactions that are applicable to them
are organized in the TCC and corresponding transaction type table.
TCC and corresponding transaction type
TCC Transaction Type
A Automobile/Vehicle Rental This TCC applies to the rental of an automobile,
bus, truck, or motor home, but does not apply to the rental of a bicycle,
motorbike, trailer, or other vehicle.
C Manual Cash Disbursement This TCC applies to a transaction in which the
cardholder receives cash or travelers’ cheques at a customer financial
institution, or cash or travelers’ cheques at the location of a qualified and
approved agent of a customer financial institution.
F Restaurant This TCC applies to transactions processed by a restaurant,
including those located in a hospital, hotel, cruise ship, or similar location.
Acceptor business codes (MCCs)
Required use of MCCs
© 2023 Mastercard. Proprietary. All rights reserved.
Quick Reference Booklet—Merchant Edition • 3 October 2023 23
TCC Transaction Type
H Hotel/Motel This TCC applies only to transactions involving the provision of
sleeping or meeting room accommodations, or both. This TCC also may
include goods and services that are included on a bill for these
accommodations by a hotel, motel, or inn, but not by any boarding house or
lodging house providing services primarily for permanent guests, and not by a
trailer or camping park.
This TCC does not apply to any apparel store, florist, gift shop, or restaurant
transaction in a hotel, motel, or inn that is not posted to a bill that includes
charges for the providing of sleeping or meeting room accommodations.
In the case of cruise ships sailing in any waters, this TCC applies only to
accumulated incidental charges that were incurred aboard ship and are
posted to an account with the shipping company that is payable upon
disembarkation. This includes transactions originating at merchant locations
aboard the ship, for example, at an apparel store, gift shop, or florist.
O College/School Expense This TCC applies only to transactions involving
charges for tuition or room and board by an institution that is a university,
college, junior college, or preparatory school. The institution must be
accredited by the regional or other appropriate accrediting authority. It must
be conducting a full-time academic program. The transaction also may
include other college/school expenses and charges, such as books, insurance,
and athletic fees.
This TCC does not apply to charges by a trade school, or any establishment
for the teaching of a particular skill or group of skills, such as a school of
design, beauticians’ school, fencing school, or computer programming school.
O Hospital This TCC applies only to transactions involving a charge for an
overnight bed occupancy by a patient. The transaction may include, in
addition to the overnight bed occupancy charge by a patient, related goods
and services. This TCC does not apply to a separate bill for outpatient service,
or any florist, gift shop, or restaurant transaction in a hospital that is not
posted to a hospital bill that includes a patient’s overnight bed occupancy
charges. A hospital is an institution for the care or treatment of persons who
are sick, injured, aged, infirm, or young, and it may be an asylum, a sanitarium,
or a rest home.
P Payment Transaction This TCC applies to Payment Transactions including
Mastercard Gaming Payment Transactions, Mastercard MoneySend Payment
Transactions and Mastercard MoneySend Payment Transactions for the
purposes of fast refunds for purchase returns. A Payment Transaction is a
transaction that transfers funds to a cardholder account. A Payment
Transaction must be authorized by the issuer.
R All Other Merchants/U.S. Post Exchange This TCC applies to those
transactions taking place at a retail store or U.S. Post Exchange.
Acceptor business codes (MCCs)
Definitions: Transaction Category Codes and types of transactions
© 2023 Mastercard. Proprietary. All rights reserved.
Quick Reference Booklet—Merchant Edition • 3 October 2023 24
TCC Transaction Type
R or U Cardholder-Activated Terminal (CAT Level 1, 2, 3, and 4) This TCC applies to
a cardholder-activated magnetic stripe-reading terminal (usually
unattended) that dispenses a product or provides a service. The terminal is
either an Automated Dispensing Machine/Level 1, Self-Service Terminal/Level
2, Limited Amount Terminal/Level 3, or In-Flight Commerce Terminal/Level 4
in accordance with Mastercard standards. For more details, refer to Appendix
D of the Transaction Processing Rules manual.
T All Other Non–Face-to-Face Transactions This TCC applies to non–face-to-
face transactions, including but not limited to recurring transactions, mail
order/telephone order transactions, electronic and mobile commerce
transactions, and transponder transactions. Recurring or preauthorized
transactions result from a specific authorization given to the merchant where
the cardholder has agreed to periodic billings submitted by the merchant. Mail
order/telephone order, electronic and mobile commerce, and transponder
transactions result from a cardholder authorizing a sale to be charged to his
or her account via a non–face-to-face method.
U Unique Transactions This TCC applies only to transactions identified with one
of the following acceptor business codes: 4829, 6050, 6051, 7995, 7801, or
7802. The TCC of “U” must be used in combination with any of these acceptor
business codes, regardless of transaction environment (with the sole
exception of Gaming Payment Transactions, which use a TCC of “P” and occur
at Europe and MEA region acceptors only).
X Airline This TCC applies to a passenger airline merchant or its authorized
agent that sells tickets on behalf of the airlines.
X Railroad This TCC applies to a passenger railroad merchant or its authorized
agent that sells tickets on behalf of the railroads.
X Travel Agency/Transportation This TCC applies to transactions involving
charges for other common carrier passenger transportation. The transaction,
in addition to these charges, may include charges that are incidental to
scheduled common carrier passenger transportation.
Z Automated Cash Disbursement This TCC applies to a transaction in which
the cardholder receives cash at an ATM.

MCC descriptions
Various MCC categories are described in the MCC descriptions table.
MCC descriptions
MCC Category Description
Airlines The Airlines category consists of air carriers and
airlines.
Amusement and Entertainment Amusement and Entertainment merchants provide
recreation and entertainment services; includes the
managers, performers, promoters, organizers,
operators, renters, and sellers of such services.
Automobile/Vehicle Rentals Automobile/Vehicle Rentals merchants provide
short-term or long-term rentals of cars, trucks,
vans, utility trailers, motor homes, or recreational
vehicles.
Automobiles and Vehicles Automobiles and Vehicles merchants sell new and
used vehicles, provide vehicle replacement parts
and accessories, sell fuel, and also may make
repairs. Vehicles sold include cars, motorcycles,
trucks, recreational trailers, motor homes,
watercraft, and snowmobiles.
Business Services Business Services merchants are typically engaged
in trades and business support services, providing
specialized goods and services for consumers and
businesses.
Clothing Stores Clothing Stores sell clothing, accessories, and other
apparel.
Contracted Services Contracted Services merchants are general and
specialized contractors that provide building,
landscape, agricultural, veterinary, and other
services.
Acceptor business codes (MCCs)
MCC descriptions
© 2023 Mastercard. Proprietary. All rights reserved.
Quick Reference Booklet—Merchant Edition • 3 October 2023 37
MCC Category Description
Government Services Government Services merchants include local,
state, and federal entities that provide
administration and processing functions, as well as
civil commissions, government accounting, supply
and services offices, and other providers of
government support services.
Hotels and Motels The Hotels and Motels category includes all lodging
establishments, such as “bed and breakfast” and
other inns, resorts, cabins, and hostels. It does not
include recreational areas in which patrons provide
their own shelter, such as campgrounds and trailer
parks.
Mail Order/Telephone Order Providers Mail Order/Telephone Order Providers use direct
marketing techniques such as mailings, advertising,
or other methods to sell products, services, and
information, or provide access to audiotext or
videotext services.
Miscellaneous Stores Miscellaneous Stores sell unique or specialized
items and services rather than a general line of
merchandise. Examples include eating and drinking
establishments, pharmacies, home furnishing,
electronics, and household appliance stores.
Personal Service Providers Personal Service Providers supply services of a
personal nature such as dry cleaning, dating, tax
preparation, funeral, clothing rental, and spa
services.
Professional Services and Membership
Organizations
The Professional Services and Membership
Organizations category includes professionals with
advanced or specialized education or training,
schools and educational services, and membership
associations and organizations.
Repair Services Repair Services merchants specialize in repair and
related services.
Retail Stores Retail Stores sell a variety of general merchandise.
Examples include building material, hardware,
garden supply, and food stores, and discount and
department stores. Merchants that primarily sell
apparel are classified under Clothing Stores. Eating
and drinking establishments are classified as
Miscellaneous Stores.
Acceptor business codes (MCCs)
MCC descriptions
© 2023 Mastercard. Proprietary. All rights reserved.
Quick Reference Booklet—Merchant Edition • 3 October 2023 38
MCC Category Description
Service Providers Service Providers supply non-personal services.
Examples include cash disbursements by financial
institutions, sales of travelers cheques and foreign
currency by non-financial institutions, insurance
sales, timeshare sales, and campground operators.
Transportation Transportation merchants include providers of
passenger and freight transportation, as well as
emergency, courier, storage, travel, and toll
collection services.
United Kingdom This category is for regional use only.
Utilities Utilities merchants provide public services such as
power, water, sanitation, telecommunications,
telegraph, pay television, computer network, and
information, and funds transfer services. Sellers of
telecommunications equipment are also included.
Wholesale Distributors and Manufacturers Wholesale Distributors and Manufacturers sell
goods and services exclusively to other businesses.
MCC Listing
The MCC Listing spreadsheet contains all acceptor business codes (MCCs).
This spreadsheet also contains domestic use-only (country-specific) MCCs. It can be saved to a
local drive to allow users to sort the information for their specific application needs.
Downloading the MCC Listing spreadsheet
From the HTML version of the Quick Reference Booklet, the user can access the MCC Listing
Microsoft Excel® file.
Procedure
1. Click the Download Attachments icon.
2. Click the file name.

Acceptor business codes (MCCs): extended
Acceptor business codes (MCCs) are listed numerically by MCC. The description for each MCC
within this section, includes the TCC(s) that are valid for that MCC. Only a valid combination of
MCC and TCC may be used in a transaction.
MCC 0742: Veterinary Services
The description of each MCC includes the TCC(s) that are valid for that MCC. Only a valid
combination of MCC and TCC may be used in a transaction.
TCC R for face-to-face transactions.
T for non–face-to-face transactions.
MCC Description Licensed practitioners primarily engaged in the practice of veterinary
medicine, dentistry, or surgery for all types of animals; such as pets
(for example, dogs, cats, fish), livestock, and other farm animals (for
example, cattle, horses, sheep, hogs, goats, poultry, bees), and exotic
animals.

MCC 4829: Money Transfer
The description of each MCC includes the TCC(s) that are valid for that MCC. Only a valid
combination of MCC and TCC may be used in a transaction.
TCC U
MCC Description A transaction in which funds are delivered or made available to a
person or to an account. These transactions include non–face-to-
face transactions such as those facilitated through the Internet.
Any fee charged and included in the total transaction amount must
be clearly disclosed to the cardholder before completing the
transaction.
The acquirer must include the identity and location of the money
transfer agent that accepts the card and effects the transaction in
the acceptor descriptor record as the site where the transaction was
effected. For more information, refer to the Mastercard MoneySend
and Funding Transactions Program Standards.

MCC 5732: Electronic Sales
The description of each MCC includes the TCC(s) that are valid for that MCC. Only a valid
combination of MCC and TCC may be used in a transaction.
TCC R for face-to-face transactions.
T for non–face-to-face transactions.
MCC Description Merchants that sell or lease a wide variety of electronic goods,
including computer hardware, and may also sell parts or accessories
for the repair, construction, or assembly of electronic equipment.
Electronic sales merchants may or may not also conduct repair work.
Products for sale may include televisions, radios, VCRs, cameras,
video cameras, stereo components, and car stereos and speakers.
For merchants that solely conduct electronics repair work, use MCC
7622.
For merchants that primarily sell household appliances such as
washing machines, clothes dryers, and refrigerators, use MCC 5722.

combination of MCC and TCC may be used in a transaction.
TCC R for face-to-face transactions.
T for non–face-to-face transactions.

cannabis. Such merchant must be properly registered with

Procedures manual.

MCC 5960: Direct Marketing: Insurance Services
The description of each MCC includes the TCC(s) that are valid for that MCC. Only a valid
combination of MCC and TCC may be used in a transaction.
TCC T for non–face-to-face transactions.
MCC Description Merchants that sell insurance services via direct mail, billing
statement stuffers, and magazine or television ads, all of which
include either a toll-free phone number or an address or Web site by
which prospective clients may respond. Insurance services offered
may include all forms of life insurance, hospital indemnity insurance
(additional coverage usually paid directly to the consumer),
accidental death and dismemberment insurance, credit card
insurance in which the outstanding balance is insured against the
cardholder’s death, disability or unemployment insurance, and
medical insurance for travelers. Sales may be targeted to special
groups such as veterans, retired persons, schoolteachers, or
members of certain organizations. The billing of the insurance
premiums typically occurs in periodic (monthly, quarterly, or annual)
installments, and continues until canceled by either the cardholder or
the insurance company. Another common feature is a free trial
period of 60 or 90 days, with the billing of the first installment after
the trial period has ended.
For face-to-face insurance sales and underwriting services, use MCC
6300.

MCC 5964: Direct Marketing: Catalog Merchants
The description of each MCC includes the TCC(s) that are valid for that MCC. Only a valid
combination of MCC and TCC may be used in a transaction.
TCC T for non–face-to-face transactions.
MCC Description Merchants that initiate direct contact with consumers and are often
described as mail-order houses or as the mail-order industry. Such
merchants offer their merchandise via catalogs, and accept
merchandise orders exclusively via mail, phone, fax, electronic
commerce, or other non–face-to-face methods. A paper catalog is a
multi-page document that is sent (mailed, faxed, or otherwise
delivered) directly to a consumer. An electronic catalog displays
merchandise via cable TV or as videotext on an Internet site.
Catalogs display and describe merchandise and include a mail-order
form, phone number, or Internet site address for placing orders.
Flyers and brochures are not considered catalogs.
A manufacturer with a pricing catalog is not considered a direct
marketing catalog merchant.
MCC Category Mail Order/Telephone Order Providers
AB Programs Global: CCR3, CR02, M001, M003
Country-specific: BEL1, BR07, BR10, COL5, CHLG,
TT01-TTO

© 2023 Mastercard. Proprietary. All rights reserved.

MCC Description Catalog merchants that also operate one or more retail outlets. This
MCC is used only for transactions occurring via mail order, phone
order, electronic commerce, or other non–face-to-face methods, even
if the merchandise is delivered to a store for pick-up.
Face-to-face sales, including those in which the order is placed at a
catalog desk or elsewhere in a store in response to a catalog or other
direct response communication are excluded from this MCC.
All retail sales must be processed under an appropriate retail MCC.

Acceptor business codes (MCCs)
MCC 5967: Direct Marketing: Inbound Telemarketing Merchants
© 2023 Mastercard. Proprietary. All rights reserved.
Quick Reference Booklet—Merchant Edition • 3 October 2023 139
MCC Description Merchants that sell subscription products or services via direct mail,
phone, the Internet, or other direct marketing method that includes
either a toll-free number, mailing address, e-mail address, or website
URL. Such merchants may offer a series of products (such as one
book a month for one year) or the annual renewal of a single
product. The cardholder’s Mastercard card account is billed for the
product or service on a continuing or periodic basis (such as once a
month or twice a year), and the product or service continues until the
subscription or series ends or the cardholder or merchant terminates
the agreement. This MCC includes book clubs, magazine and
newspaper subscriptions, audio clubs selling records, tapes, and
compact discs (CDs), video tape and digital video disc (DVD) clubs,
collectible series subscriptions (for example, series of stamps, coins,
books, plates, china figures, or plates), magazine subscriptions,
health-care product subscriptions, cosmetics subscriptions, vitamin
subscriptions, and credit card registration service companies.
For newspaper classified ads sold via direct marketing methods, use
MCC 5969.
An acquirer must use this MCC to identify transactions arising from
a high-risk negative option billing merchant selling physical products.
Such merchant must be properly registered with Mastercard as set
forth in section 9.4.10 of the Security Rules and Procedures manual.
Recurring transactions excluded from this category include utility
payments (use MCC 4900), private athletic club monthly dues (use
MCC 7997), and insurance premiums (use MCC 6300).

MCC Description Merchants that sell products and services through a variety of direct
response methods in which an order form or an address or phone

fax. These merchants often use mass-marketing techniques such as

MCC 7922.

phone orders for customer convenience.

appropriate retail MCC with a TCC of T.

MCC 6010: Manual Cash Disbursements: Customer Financial Institution
The description of each MCC includes the TCC(s) that are valid for that MCC. Only a valid
combination of MCC and TCC may be used in a transaction.
TCC C
MCC Description Used only to identify face-to-face transactions in which a cardholder
uses a Mastercard card at a Mastercard customer financial
institution to obtain a manual (“over-the-counter”) cash
disbursement, to open or fund a deposit account, or to purchase
travelers cheques, foreign currency, money orders, precious metals, or
savings bonds.
For cash disbursement transactions occurring at automated teller
machines (ATMs), use MCC 6011.
For sales of foreign currency, money orders, travelers cheques, and
other quasi-cash products at locations other than Mastercard
customer financial institution locations, use MCC 6051.
MCC Category Service Providers
AB Programs Global: C001
Country-specific: BR07, BR10, CHLG

Acceptor business codes (MCCs)
MCC 6012: Merchandise and Services: Customer Financial Institution
© 2023 Mastercard. Proprietary. All rights reserved.
Quick Reference Booklet—Merchant Edition • 3 October 2023 153
MCC Description Identifies the purchase, with a Mastercard or Maestro card, of
travelers cheques, foreign currency, money orders, precious metals, or
savings bonds at a Mastercard customer financial institution
location. This MCC may also be used to identify transactions in which
a customer accepts a Mastercard or Maestro card in direct payment
of an existing debt, such as a private label card or vehicle loan.
This MCC may be used for non–face-to-face transactions, such as
those facilitated through the Internet.
MCC 6050 must not be used to identify any sale other than as
described, including, by way of example and not limitation; gambling
transactions (MCC 7995, MCC 7801, or MCC 7802, as appropriate,
must be used); videotext transactions (MCC 5967 must be used);
the sale of any prescription drug (MCC 5122 or MCC 5912 must be
used); or the sale of any tobacco product (MCC 5993 must be used).
Any fee charged and included in the total transaction amount must
be clearly disclosed to the cardholder before completing the
transaction.
For cash disbursements, use MCC 6010 for face-to-face
transactions and MCC 6011 for transactions that occur at ATMs.
MCC Category Service Providers
AB Programs Global: CCR1, CR05, T002, U001
Country-specific: BR07, BR10, CHLG, COLM

transaction.

MCC 6532: Payment Transaction: Customer Financial Institution
The description in of each MCC includes the TCC(s) that are valid for that MCC. Only a valid
combination of MCC and TCC may be used in a transaction.
TCC P
MCC Description This MCC may be used only to identify Payment Transactions as
stated below. A Payment Transaction is a transfer of funds to a
Mastercard, Maestro, or Cirrus account by means of the Mastercard
network. For more information, refer to section 6.1 of the
Transaction Processing Rules.
NOTE: This MCC must only be used for rePower value loads or
specified domestic payments, in combination with one of the
following Transaction Type Identifier (TTI) values as applicable:
• C02 Mastercard rebate
• C03 rePower Load Value
• C06 Payment of a credit card balance with cash or check (for
Colombia domestic use only)
• C91 Utility Payments (for Brazil domestic use only)
• C92 Government Services (for Brazil domestic use only)
• C93 Mobile phone top-ups (for Brazil domestic use only)
• C94 Coupon booklet payments (for Brazil domestic use only)
For information about TTI usage, refer to DE 48, subelement 77
(Transaction Type Identifier) in the Customer Interface Specification
and Single Message Specifications manuals and PDS 0043
(Transaction Type Identifier) in the IPM Clearing Formats manual.
MCC Category Service Providers
AB Programs Global: D001

MCC 6540: Funding Transactions
The description of each MCC includes the TCC(s) that are valid for that MCC. Only a valid
combination of MCC and TCC may be used in a transaction.
TCC R for face-to-face transactions.
T for non-face-to-face transactions.
MCC Description Identifies a Funding Transaction, as described in section 6.6 of the
Transaction Processing Rules.
MCC 6540 must not be used to identify a Funding Transaction
conducted for purposes of funding any of the activities described in
section 9.1 of the Security Rules and Procedures manual (the
appropriate MCC for each such activity must be used).
Funding Transactions must comply with the requirements set out in
the Standards, including the Mastercard MoneySend and Funding
Transaction Program Standards.

MON3, OTH1, OTH2, OTH3,
OTH4, OTH5

OT34, OT36, OT41

© 2023 Mastercard. Proprietary. All rights reserved.
Quick Reference Booklet—Merchant Edition • 3 October 2023 180
MCC Description Merchants that provide housekeeping or intermediary service to
family. Housekeeping services usually include nanny, nurse, cook,
gardener, driver, guard, tutor service to a family.
For merchants that provide employment services for employers or
those seeking employment with permanent or temporary positions,
use MCC 7361.
For merchants funded by the government, provide care and help
services specially for the elderly, five guarantees family, disabled
people, disabled children, use MCC 9399.
Business Services merchants are typically engaged in trades and
business support services, providing specialized goods and services
for consumers and businesses.
All Other Merchants/U.S. Post Exchange
This TCC applies to those transactions taking place at a retail store
or U.S. Post Exchange.
All Other Non–Face-to-Face Transactions
This TCC applies to non–face-to-face transactions, including but not
limited to recurring transactions, mail order/telephone order
transactions, electronic and mobile commerce transactions, and
transponder transactions. Recurring or preauthorized transactions
result from a specific authorization given to the merchant where the
cardholder has agreed to periodic billings submitted by the
merchant. Mail order/telephone order, electronic and mobile
commerce, and transponder transactions result from a cardholder
authorizing a sale to be charged to his or her account via a non–face-
to-face method.
Customers must not use this MCC for cross-border transactions.

TCC P for Gaming Payment transactions.

MCC Description Merchants that operate indoor playgrounds, interactive games and

instant photograph booths.

merchant or a skill games merchant located outside the U.S. region
that accepts payment from U.S. region cardholders for participation
in a skill game conducted by such merchant. Such merchant must be
properly registered with Mastercard as set forth in section 9.4.5 of
the Security Rules and Procedures manual. If such merchant's
activities are regulated as gambling in any non-U.S. jurisdiction, then
the merchant must be identified with MCC 7995.
For merchants that sell amusement equipment, use MCC 7993.
For merchants that operate games involving wagering, use MCC
7995.

MCC 7995: Gambling Transactions
The description in each MCC includes the TCC(s) that are valid for that MCC. Only a valid
combination of MCC and TCC may be used in a transaction.
TCC P for Gaming Payment transactions.
U for purchases of gambling chips or other value usable for
gambling.
MCC Description Any transaction, other than an ATM transaction, involving the placing
of a wager, the purchase of a lottery ticket, spread betting, in-flight
commerce gaming, or the purchase of chips or other value usable for
gambling in conjunction with gambling activities provided by
wagering or betting establishments such as casinos, race tracks, card
parlors, airlines, and the like.
Gambling transaction processing requirements are set forth in
section 5.1.2.2 of the Mastercard Rules manual.
Any fee charged and included in the total transaction amount must
be clearly disclosed to the cardholder before completing the
transaction. Such a fee must not be charged for in-flight commerce
gaming transactions.
Before acquiring transactions reflecting non-face-to-face gambling,
an acquirer must first register the merchant with Mastercard as
described in section 9.2 of the Security Rules and Procedures manual.
For other types of purchases associated with the establishment,
such as food, lodging, or passage, use the MCC that best describes
that transaction.
For information about Gaming Payment Transactions, refer to
Chapter 6 in the Transaction Processing Rules manual.
MCC Category Amusement and Entertainment
AB Programs Global: CCR1, CR05, U001
Country-specific: BEL1, BR07, BR10, CHLE, CHLM,
COLM, GAM1, JA02, SPN4,
TT01-TTO, U003
Acceptor business codes (MCCs)

© 2023 Mastercard. Proprietary. All rights reserved.

The description of each MCC includes the TCC(s) that are valid for that MCC. Only a valid
combination of MCC and TCC may be used in a transaction.
TCC R for face-to-face transactions.
T for non–face-to-face transactions.
MCC Description Merchants that operate sports and recreation facilities requiring
membership. Examples of such facilities include exercise, athletic,
and health clubs, country clubs, private golf courses, boating yacht
clubs, swimming clubs, tennis clubs, bowling leagues, riding clubs,
shooting and gun clubs, and racquetball clubs. Such merchants may
or may not provide massage services and spa services such as facials,
weight control counseling, aromatherapy, steam baths, and
whirlpools.
For merchants that primarily provide massages, use MCC 7297.
For merchants that primarily operate a spa and its related services,
use MCC 7298.

MCC Description Merchants that provide a wide variety of recreation and

MCC 8042: Optometrists, Ophthalmologists
The description of each MCC includes the TCC(s) that are valid for that MCC. Only a valid
combination of MCC and TCC may be used in a transaction.
TCC R for face-to-face transactions.
T for non–face-to-face transactions.
MCC Description Optometrists are medical professionals that examine and treat eye
defects with corrective lenses or exercises. Ophthalmologists are
licensed physicians that specialize in the structures, functions, and
diseases of the eye, and may perform surgery. These merchants may
or may not fill eyeglass or contact lens prescriptions, or sell eyeglass
frames.

MCC Description Merchants that read prescriptions for visual correction, order lenses,

cases, and eyeglass and contact lens solutions. One-hour eyeglasses
merchants generally located in shopping malls are included.
For merchants that examine eyes and treat eye defects with

8042.

MCC Description Merchants that provide general support services to the government
such as personnel, auditing, procurement, and building management
services, and are not described by another, more specific MCC.

government accounting offices, general services offices, government
supply agencies, police, fire, and motor vehicle departments, and
national, state, and city parks.

MCC 9405.

government should use the wholesale MCC that best describes the
business.

MCC Description A lottery scheme conducted and managed by a government
authority. Use of this MCC is restricted to the following regions:
Asia/Pacific, Canada, Europe, Latin America and the Caribbean, and
Middle East/Africa. Merchants located in the U.S. region should use
MCC 7800: Government Owned Lottery (U.S. region only).
NOTE: Use of MCC 9406 is appropriate to identify a duly licensed
agent engaged in the sale of lottery tickets, reoccurring lottery
subscription services, or both.
